  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_5dc56dac-f8a3-4d10-90f6-82241e87fd6a'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

<span id="freeTextContainer4259638209791791264">Not even the icy temperatures of a typical New England winter can match the bone-chilling scene of carnage discovered at the chapel of Our Lady of Divine Light. Within the cloistered convent lie two nuns–one dead, one critically injured–victims of an unspeakably savage attacker. The brutal crime appears to be without motive, but medical examiner Maura Isles’s autopsy of th</span>
  <span id="freeText4259638209791791264" style="display:none">Not even the icy temperatures of a typical New England winter can match the bone-chilling scene of carnage discovered at the chapel of Our Lady of Divine Light. Within the cloistered convent lie two nuns–one dead, one critically injured–victims of an unspeakably savage attacker. The brutal crime appears to be without motive, but medical examiner Maura Isles’s autopsy of the dead woman yields a shocking surprise: Twenty-year-old Sister Camille gave birth before she was murdered. Then another body is found, mutilated beyond recognition. Together, Isles and homicide detective Jane Rizzoli uncover an ancient horror that connects these terrible slaughters. As long-buried secrets come to light, Maura Isles finds herself drawn inexorably toward the heart of an investigation that strikes close to home–and toward a dawning revelation about the killer’s identity too shattering to consider.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4259638209791791264" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4876540-jonetta?shelf=audio-2000">audio-2000</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4876540-jonetta?shelf=mystery-suspense">mystery-suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4876540-jonetta?shelf=12800-in-2018">12800-in-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4876540-jonetta?shelf=5000-books">5000-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer415768853" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7992170829775943302">It all starts with the murder of a nun within her abbey along with the assault on another. As Jane Rizzoli and Maura Isles investigate, it leads them toward some highly surprising and divergent paths, including connections to other circumstances. <br/><br/>This is the book where we learn more about Maura Isles, finally. Her voice is the strongest though Jane gets considerable space. Nicknamed the <i>Queen of the Dead</i> because of what she does and her gothic look, Maura had to be more complex than a caricature</span>
  <span id="freeText7992170829775943302" style="display:none">It all starts with the murder of a nun within her abbey along with the assault on another. As Jane Rizzoli and Maura Isles investigate, it leads them toward some highly surprising and divergent paths, including connections to other circumstances. <br /><br />This is the book where we learn more about Maura Isles, finally. Her voice is the strongest though Jane gets considerable space. Nicknamed the <i>Queen of the Dead</i> because of what she does and her gothic look, Maura had to be more complex than a caricature (she is) and that unfolds. And, her relationship with Jane Rizzoli develops beyond their roles of detective and medical examiner. <br /><br />There were also personal elements for both that added texture to them as characters and the story. Both became more relatable here because of it and their work dynamics played out well. I really liked the story because of this and the complexity of the cases. I was a little blindsighted by the excellent twists at the end though the clues were there. I also listened to the story and Anna Fields did a great job but her pronunciation of Jane’s last name (Ritz-zoli) drove me nuts. Otherwise, this was a very good reading experience. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7992170829775943302" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2297917451" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2297917451" />
    <a title="Sarah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7477266-sarah"><img alt="Sarah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1433820623p2/7477266.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2297917451?book_show_action=true">Feb 19, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah" href="/user/show/7477266-sarah">Sarah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/5339010-the-sinner">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7477266-sarah?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7477266-sarah?shelf=z2018">z2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7477266-sarah?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2297917451" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8441842592090490134">3.5 Stars. (Review contains slight spoilers for books 1 and 2 of the series). <br/><br/>Honestly, I didn't enjoy this as much as book 1 & 2. It was different to the others because instead of heavily relying on the surgeon (and the apprentice), it focused on Rizzoli & Isles solving a few cases and dealing with personal issues. I did find it weird that Rizzoli didn't really think of the Surgeon at all. He went from dominating the first two books, to disappearing and I know it might be because she doesn't se</span>
  <span id="freeText8441842592090490134" style="display:none">3.5 Stars. (Review contains slight spoilers for books 1 and 2 of the series). <br /><br />Honestly, I didn't enjoy this as much as book 1 &amp; 2. It was different to the others because instead of heavily relying on the surgeon (and the apprentice), it focused on Rizzoli &amp; Isles solving a few cases and dealing with personal issues. I did find it weird that Rizzoli didn't really think of the Surgeon at all. He went from dominating the first two books, to disappearing and I know it might be because she doesn't see him as a threat anymore but I just found it odd. I did miss the Surgeon's perspective and I missed that dynamic they had because that is probably one of the best aspects of the series. So instead of getting the Surgeon's POV, we got Maura Isles' POV alongside Rizzoli's. Unfortunately I didn't really like her. I found her intriguing in book 1 &amp; 2, but it turns out getting access to her internal monologue wasn't what I thought it would be. She's quite similar to Rizzoli but she lacks the likeability and I didn't find her interesting. I kind of wish that it was just Rizzoli's POV in this book because reading Isles' POV just made me like the book less. <br /><br />I thought the story was interesting enough but I thought the story was hijacked by each woman's love/personal life. I did think that the second half of the book was better because that is when everything started to connect and really make sense. I did wish that the crime aspect was more prominent and more developed. It was quite predictable which was unfortunate but I thought Gerritsen had a really good idea. I also didn't find the writing as enjoyable (not sure if that had to do with me not enjoying Isles' POV or if it just wasn't as good). I read this book because I wanted something that was quite addictive but it didn't fully deliver. I still think this is a good series and I will keep reading on. Hopefully I just grow to like Isles as a character. <br /><br />I know it sounds like I'm sort of bashing this book but I did give it 3.5 stars, which isn't bad and I did enjoy it. I guess I was just a little disappointed because I know how good Gerritsen can write and this just wasn't up there for me. I would recommend this series.<br /><br />--------------------------------------<br /><br />"There would be comfort in it, she thought. The ease of knowing, at each dawn, how the day will go. No surprises, no turmoil." </span>
  <a data-text-id="8441842592090490134" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2251458460" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2251458460" />
    <a title="Jean" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28831526-jean"><img alt="Jean" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1579801852p2/28831526.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2251458460?book_show_action=true">Jan 09, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jean" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jean" href="/user/show/28831526-jean">Jean</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780345458919" href="/book/show/846113.The_Sinner">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2251458460" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5560727507819174220">“Bless me, Father, for I have sinned.” No one comes out and says those words in Tess Gerritsen’s <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32257.The_Sinner__Rizzoli___Isles___3_' title='The Sinner (Rizzoli & Isles, #3) by Tess Gerritsen' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Sinner</a>. This is the third suspense novel in her Rizzoli and Isles series, and I confess, it’s a practically a sin that I haven’t gotten around to reading this book until now. It’s been three years since I read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/715834.The_Apprentice__Rizzoli___Isles___2_' title='The Apprentice (Rizzoli & Isles, #2) by Tess Gerritsen' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Apprentice</a>, and as many avid thriller mystery readers know, there are so many amazing books out there just waiting to be read that it’s hard to get to even a small percentage of them. N</span>
  <span id="freeText5560727507819174220" style="display:none">“Bless me, Father, for I have sinned.” No one comes out and says those words in Tess Gerritsen’s <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32257.The_Sinner__Rizzoli___Isles___3_" title="The Sinner (Rizzoli &amp; Isles, #3) by Tess Gerritsen" rel="nofollow noopener">The Sinner</a>. This is the third suspense novel in her Rizzoli and Isles series, and I confess, it’s a practically a sin that I haven’t gotten around to reading this book until now. It’s been three years since I read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/715834.The_Apprentice__Rizzoli___Isles___2_" title="The Apprentice (Rizzoli &amp; Isles, #2) by Tess Gerritsen" rel="nofollow noopener">The Apprentice</a>, and as many avid thriller mystery readers know, there are so many amazing books out there just waiting to be read that it’s hard to get to even a small percentage of them. Now that I’ve returned to Gerritsen’s series, I won’t be waiting another three years to read the next one.<br /><br />The first two books focused primarily on Detective Jane Rizzoli. This time around, we get to know Medical Examiner Dr. Maura Isles a lot better. Called "the Queen of the Dead" by medical students and some of the staff, Maura is a dedicated pathologist who believes that she has a duty to the deceased. She is calm in the face of the most gruesome crime scenes, a controlled, efficient professional. Rizzoli, on the other hand, is testy these days. She’s tired, cranky, and not feeling like herself. It’s days before Christmas, and the winter weather and holiday stress is getting to her. Must be the flu, she says.<br /><br />When they are called to a crime scene at an abbey for a contemplative order of nuns, Rizzoli and Isles face challenges different from any they have faced before. These are women who do not venture out into the world except on rare occasions. Who would want to harm any of them, much less kill them? These are women of faith. Dr. Isles is a person of science. Detective Rizzoli, too, wants answers the sisters cannot give because their faith simply does not let them imagine the possibilities. Can there be a middle ground?<br /><br />As a medical examiner in the Boston area, Dr. Isles has more than one case, naturally. What are the chances that she would have another death related to the murder at the convent? Little by little, Tess Gerritsen weaves her story. Along the way, she reveals some secrets. I was feeling proud of myself for figuring things out as I went along. I was putting two and two together and getting four. So far, so good. As for the main piece of the puzzle, however, I was waiting for that one big aha moment when I would have at least an inkling. I did, actually, and it was a good hunch, but I was slightly off the mark. Only slightly. <br /><br />Do we find out what was bugging Jane Rizzoli those days leading up to Christmas? Read the book. And better yet, to find out if there is any passion and joy under that “Queen of the Dead” mask that Maura Isles wears, read the book. Who killed Sister Camille – and why? Read the book.<br /><br />I’m glad I did, and I look forward to continuing this series very soon!<br /><br />5 stars</span>
  <a data-text-id="5560727507819174220" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText13425868959136929488" style="display:none">Another well-written entry in Gerritsen’s Rizzoli and Isles series... even though this is really the first time we get a chance to meet the ultra professional ME Maura Isles, I finally understand what folks like about their match up. <br /><br />And even if the mystery was actually a bit cliched (I won’t give it away but you’ll know what I mean when you read it), it was still an interesting mix of characters — victims and villains alike. <br /><br />I especially liked that Jane Rizzoli’s life is changing as Maura Isles is introduced to readers. <div id="review_2584398434" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2584398434" />
    <a title="Jim" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36199787-jim"><img alt="Jim" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1445213837p2/36199787.jpg" /></a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/39891548-the-sinner">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36199787-jim?shelf=mystery-suspense-thriller">mystery-suspense-thriller</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2584398434" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7985623601550865378">The third book in the Rizzoli & Isles series and we get to know the characters better. Especially Maura Isles who until this book seemed to have more of a supporting role. The story opens with Isles performing an autopsy when she receives a call from detective Jane Rizzoli asking her to come to a crime scene.<br/><br/>The scene is the chapel of Our Lady of Divine Light, a cloistered convent. There two nuns were savagely attacked. 20 year old Sister Camille is dead. The other is critically injured. Who wou</span>
  <span id="freeText7985623601550865378" style="display:none">The third book in the Rizzoli &amp; Isles series and we get to know the characters better. Especially Maura Isles who until this book seemed to have more of a supporting role. The story opens with Isles performing an autopsy when she receives a call from detective Jane Rizzoli asking her to come to a crime scene.<br /><br />The scene is the chapel of Our Lady of Divine Light, a cloistered convent. There two nuns were savagely attacked. 20 year old Sister Camille is dead. The other is critically injured. Who would attack nuns? And why? Sister Ursula is too badly injured to talk. Sister Camille is dead but maybe she can tell Maura Isles what happened. During the autopsy Dr. Isles makes a shocking discovery. Sister Camille had recently given birth. Who is the father? A suspect obviously.<br /><br />With the exception of Sister Camille the sisters at Our Lady of Divine Light are all elderly and cannot help in the investigation but there is one person who no one really pays any attention to. Noni, the daughter of the cook / housekeeper, may be young but she is very observant and provides some invaluable clues. Then another body is found, mutilated beyond recognition. An attempt to hide the identity?<br /><br />As Rizzoli and Isles continue their investigations into the deaths a link is discovered. A secret that someone is going to great lengths to make sure remains hidden. Things are not always what they seem at first. Maura Isles finds the crimes hit close to home. She is known as the "Queen of the Dead" because of her work and goth appearance but she had a life before she became a medical examiner in Boston. In this story we get to know more about that life and I found myself liking her more. The reader also learns about a change in Jane Rizzoli's life and a decision she will have to make.<br /><br />I enjoyed this book very much and recommend it to anyone who enjoys the thriller / suspense genre. Especially those with strong female leads.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7985623601550865378" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_81157142" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/81157142" />
    <a title="Raíla" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3017047-ra-la"><img alt="Raíla" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1595187006p2/3017047.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/81157142?book_show_action=true">Dec 15, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Raíla" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Raíla" href="/user/show/3017047-ra-la">Raíla</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3017047-ra-la?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3017047-ra-la?shelf=reviews-written">reviews-written</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer81157142" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15892338668633866366">Even though I have already read and reviewed The Surgeon and The Apprentice, Tess' previous books in the series, I still feel that it's such a perkiness of mine to review any book written by this genious (I emphasize: genious!). Gerritsen, one more time, now through The Sinner, made me hook into her writing until the end, NOT letting me to put it down, despite a few flaws I found that I dare myself to point again.<br/><br/>A crime envolving two nuns, in the circuntances presented by Jane and Maura therewi</span>
  <span id="freeText15892338668633866366" style="display:none">Even though I have already read and reviewed The Surgeon and The Apprentice, Tess' previous books in the series, I still feel that it's such a perkiness of mine to review any book written by this genious (I emphasize: genious!). Gerritsen, one more time, now through The Sinner, made me hook into her writing until the end, NOT letting me to put it down, despite a few flaws I found that I dare myself to point again.<br /><br />A crime envolving two nuns, in the circuntances presented by Jane and Maura therewith the investigation of the case, conduces us to initially match the name of the book to the probable "nickname" that could characterize one of the victims. However, two more crimes — a woman that can't be identified plus a massacre in a village in India years before — come to the surface and probably discard any previously settled teory by the readers about the ending of the story. Also, it's disclosed that the three crimes are, at last, all connected.<br /><br />During several pages of the book, we're shown Maure Isles' life in and out of the morgue more throughly. It's soon noticed that the focus is aimed at introducing the patologist as a protagonist of the series — just like the policialwoman-detective Jane Rizzoli is in the previous book, The Apprentice.<br /><br />This point of introducing one more protagonist into the series can turn it into a tiring reading at certain moments. Besides, can shadow the awesomeness the ending could have had — knowing the talent of Tess Gerritsen as a writer — and conduce the readers not to enjoy the book, but to even let them a little disappointed.<br /><br />Nothing of this, though, mean that being acquainted more deeply with the character has turned The Sinner into a wearisome book. On the contrary: I've met a less cold and "self-loved" Jane Rizzoli, intimately braver to relieve everything, accepting her mistakes and wills, and to push off all the fear and weakness she denied to have. I've also met a new friend, Maura, who shows to be a better positive person, with a big heart, but not allowed to feel completely happy, considering her familiar, relationships problems. We get to, soon, relate ourselves to Maura and Jane, two protagonists that we, certainly, will miss once we have to say goodbye.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15892338668633866366" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2734812259" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1362856432342493397">If you haven't noticed, I'm obsessed with this series. Despite how different the books are from the tv show, reading them really makes me want to binge watch the show ( I need to see if its streaming anywhere). <br/><br/>The Sinner is about the death of a 20 year old nun and the nearly fatal assault of an elderly nun. While investigating Rizzoli and Isles discover the dead nun had recently given birth(not a spoiler, that's on the back cover). <br/><br/>I was happy to finally get more Maura Isles. The first two book</span>
  <span id="freeText1362856432342493397" style="display:none">If you haven't noticed, I'm obsessed with this series. Despite how different the books are from the tv show, reading them really makes me want to binge watch the show ( I need to see if its streaming anywhere). <br /><br />The Sinner is about the death of a 20 year old nun and the nearly fatal assault of an elderly nun. While investigating Rizzoli and Isles discover the dead nun had recently given birth(not a spoiler, that's on the back cover). <br /><br />I was happy to finally get more Maura Isles. The first two books contain very little Isles but in The Sinner we get a Isles center storyline involving her ex-husband. The murder mystery at the heart of this book wasn't as interesting as the first two books but the character development of Jane Rizzoli and Maura Isles more than made up for it. Jane's storyline is the B-story but could just as easily been the main storyline. <br /><br />I'm really enjoying this series and I really needed this book last night after watching All 4 hours of Leaving Neverland. This book served as a stress reliever.<br /><br />If you're looking for a female centered crime series I think you'll love the Rizzoli &amp; Isles series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1362856432342493397" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7021685341138855842">A complex case for Jane Rizzoli and Maura Isles with some red herrings thrown in. The case kicks off in with the violent assault of two nuns in a convent, leaving one dead and one grievously injured. One has recently returned from India and one is new to the order and has a shameful secret - but is that the reason they were attacked? The gruesome find of a hideously mutilated body in an abandoned building also keeps Rizzoli and Isles busy. Both must also deal with their love lives as Maura's ex </span>
  <span id="freeText7021685341138855842" style="display:none">A complex case for Jane Rizzoli and Maura Isles with some red herrings thrown in. The case kicks off in with the violent assault of two nuns in a convent, leaving one dead and one grievously injured. One has recently returned from India and one is new to the order and has a shameful secret - but is that the reason they were attacked? The gruesome find of a hideously mutilated body in an abandoned building also keeps Rizzoli and Isles busy. Both must also deal with their love lives as Maura's ex husband turns up wanting a second chance and Jane must confront her feelings about FBI agent Gabriel Dean. After some twists and turns and some top class investigative and forensic detective work a shocking international cover-up is discovered, but not before a thrilling ending.</span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11828590-eric?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11828590-eric?shelf=mystery-cop">mystery-cop</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11828590-eric?shelf=2018-reading-challenge">2018-reading-challenge</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2231538267" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17312898071874112629"><i>The Sinner</i> is a macabre thriller. If you have a vivid imagination, this book will probably gross you out in parts. Besides, "the case" Rizzoli and Isles have some personal dilemmas to face. This is perhaps the best book of this series I have read so far.<br/><br/>This is a well written murder mystery featuring Rizzoli, the tough female detective, and her colleague and friend, Isles. Maura Isles is the Medical Examiner (ME) who "processes" the dead involved in violent crimes. In this story, a brutal murder</span>
  <span id="freeText17312898071874112629" style="display:none"><i>The Sinner</i> is a macabre thriller. If you have a vivid imagination, this book will probably gross you out in parts. Besides, "the case" Rizzoli and Isles have some personal dilemmas to face. This is perhaps the best book of this series I have read so far.<br /><br />This is a well written murder mystery featuring Rizzoli, the tough female detective, and her colleague and friend, Isles. Maura Isles is the Medical Examiner (ME) who "processes" the dead involved in violent crimes. In this story, a brutal murder occurs involving two nuns in a Catholic convent. Rizzoli and Isles are called to the crime scene.<br /><br />The author takes the reader through the processing of clues. There are many twists and turns and a few a false leads that I was suckered into. In spite of the story time frame being set at Christmas, there is little cheer in the story until the very end. I found I could relate to this sentiment. I also found my mouth watering at the description of the Christmas dinner being prepared at the Jane Rizzoli's parents house.<br /><br />Here's a story where I was totally absorbed in the mystery and its characters.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17312898071874112629" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3538501102" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3538501102" />
    <a title="fleurette" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4692637-fleurette"><img alt="fleurette" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1357165343p2/4692637.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3538501102?book_show_action=true">Sep 08, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="fleurette" class="user" itemprop="url" name="fleurette" href="/user/show/4692637-fleurette">fleurette</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4692637-fleurette?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3538501102" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6704568064509119230">Good, solid story with some interesting threads and twists.<br/><br/>Like many other people, I watched the Rizzoli and Isles TV show and quite liked it. Although it wasn't the TV show that made me start reading these books. I knew about this series before and read other books by this author. And even though I was aware that the show is very, very loosely based on the book series, it still surprised me a lot when I read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32263.The_Surgeon__Rizzoli___Isles___1_' title='The Surgeon (Rizzoli & Isles, #1) by Tess Gerritsen' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Surgeon</a> how many differences there are. This is my second book in this series and t</span>
  <span id="freeText6704568064509119230" style="display:none">Good, solid story with some interesting threads and twists.<br /><br />Like many other people, I watched the Rizzoli and Isles TV show and quite liked it. Although it wasn't the TV show that made me start reading these books. I knew about this series before and read other books by this author. And even though I was aware that the show is very, very loosely based on the book series, it still surprised me a lot when I read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32263.The_Surgeon__Rizzoli___Isles___1_" title="The Surgeon (Rizzoli &amp; Isles, #1) by Tess Gerritsen" rel="nofollow noopener">The Surgeon</a> how many differences there are. This is my second book in this series and this time I was even more prepared. And yet I was surprised again. However this time at least the book was focused on the work of Rizzoli and Isles.<br /><br />From reading the first book in this series, I remember that I didn't like Rizzoli very much and I generally had a problem with poor knowledge of the characters. And this problem is at least partially solved in this book. I'm not convinced that I like Rizzoli or Isles now, but at least I got to know them much better. And I can say with full conviction that they are interesting and complicated characters that add a lot to this story.<br /><br />And the story is quite good, though maybe not as scandalous as a dead nun in a closed order would suggest. The full potential of this thread seems not to be fully used, but when I read the book, I had no problem with it. The solutions invented by the author are interesting and not obvious. There are a few things I didn't expect. And the whole story flows smoothly and without unnecessary lengthy fragments. Everything has its purpose. The action is swift and fast-paced with numerous twists and turns.<br /><br />I am also satisfied with the ending, I mean solving the case, or actually a few cases. As for the events in the personal lives of Rizzoli and Isles, and especially Rizzoli, I have mixed feelings. But this is probably mainly due to the fact that I am surprised by this thread. I don't think I know Rizzoli well enough yet to be involved in her life. But it might be interesting in the next books. At the moment, I think I like Isles more, I find her more interesting.<br /><br />This book has definitely encouraged me to read the others in this series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6704568064509119230" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText7092114876119179874" style="display:none"><b>4.5/5</b><br /><br />First there was Detective Jane Rizzoli, then you were introduced to Maura Isles. Now you get to know her more as Tess Gerritsen tells you a part of the story through her point of view. You get to see where she lives and how she works beyond the operating table in the Office of the Chief Medical Examiner.<br />Two nuns were attacked in a Convent, one a young runaway from a family of skeptics and the other is an old-aged humanitarian. Each had a deep dark secret, but who was the reason for the attack?<br />In Maura's personal life, she is reunited with her ex, a philanthropist doctor, who just happens to be home for the holidays. While Jane, the investigating Detective on the case has been feeling sick for the last few days and the reason of her sickness is something she rather not have her colleagues know about. Especially not Agent Gabriel Dean, the FBI Agent who helped her in <i>The Apprentice</i>.<br />Lepers, a corporate scam, religion, love and family are some of the topics that come up in this excellent page-turner that surpasses the previous book.😍</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10207602757284798645">Rare is the thriller that can scare me enough to leave the lights on at night, while bringing me to tears. The Sinner did both.   <span id="freeText10207602757284798645" style="display:none">Rare is the thriller that can scare me enough to leave the lights on at night, while bringing me to tears. The Sinner did both. Filled with more twists and turns than a labyrinth, The Sinner throws a curve at both Jane Rizzoli and ME Maura Isles. Jane must deal with a huge obstacle in her life as well as her relationship with Gabriel Dean, and Maura must face her own ghosts in the form of her ex-husband. <br /><br />This book serves as a pivotal point in the character development of both women, and is a must-read if you are a follower of the series. <br /><br />The mystery itself is tantalizing and surprising. No plot spoilers here -- you must read it yourself to see how the death of two nuns in Boston relates to a terrorist attack on a colony of lepers in India. A true page-turner.</span>

<div id="review_457789329" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/457789329" />
    <a title="Melissa Griffith" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6836830-melissa-griffith"><img alt="Melissa Griffith" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1378410344p2/6836830.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/457789329?book_show_action=true">Nov 17, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa Griffith" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa Griffith" href="/user/show/6836830-melissa-griffith">Melissa Griffith</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780345458919" href="/book/show/846113.The_Sinner">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer457789329" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9036780647976953186">I've read Tess Gerritsen's first two Rizzoli and Isles books before this one. I really love the way that the case progresses and keeps you hooked in those two. This one, while still very interesting, is a very abrupt change from the first two books. And while I read both of the first two in five days, this one took me almost six weeks because when I set it down, I didn't feel all that strong of a need to pick it back up.<br/><br/>Between book two and this one, the setting moves from a blistering summer to</span>
  <span id="freeText9036780647976953186" style="display:none">I've read Tess Gerritsen's first two Rizzoli and Isles books before this one. I really love the way that the case progresses and keeps you hooked in those two. This one, while still very interesting, is a very abrupt change from the first two books. And while I read both of the first two in five days, this one took me almost six weeks because when I set it down, I didn't feel all that strong of a need to pick it back up.<br /><br />Between book two and this one, the setting moves from a blistering summer to an almost intolerably cold winter, which really suits moving from the point of view of the passionate Rizzoli to the cool and logical Isles. However, I feel like they didn't start making the connections in the case that I had made in the beginning of the book until after page 200 (of 342 for my version). The case itself moved much more slowly and there was a lot more of the personal lives of the characters.<br /><br />This would be fine except... I don't really like the characters that much. Isles is okay, but a bit too poetically grand in her thoughts sometimes. And Rizzoli is just incredibly, annoyingly abrasive and whiny. Maybe it's just me, but the characters at this part of the story are just a bit too exaggerated.<br /><br />In the end, this is a crime thriller where the crime is not nearly thrilling enough; a medical thriller with barely any medical aspect to it; and a practice in exploring characters that I didn't like. However, I liked the first two so much that I intend to read the next book as it sounds much more interesting.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9036780647976953186" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3351819172" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3351819172" />
    <a title="Ian" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13985162-ian"><img alt="Ian" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594126645p2/13985162.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3351819172?book_show_action=true">May 28, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ian" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ian" href="/user/show/13985162-ian">Ian</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3351819172" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer505127205690764191">After thoroughly enjoying book 1 and 2 in TG's 'Rizzoli and Isles' series, I decided to set myself on a mission - to read all of these books within the year, and in the right chronological order. So what did I make of 'The Sinner'? Well, unfortunately I am disappointed to have to report that I found it much weaker and far less appealing than the previous novels as it felt like going 'one step forward, two steps back'. Like the other books, the opening was very strong, interesting and original, s</span>
  <span id="freeText505127205690764191" style="display:none">After thoroughly enjoying book 1 and 2 in TG's 'Rizzoli and Isles' series, I decided to set myself on a mission - to read all of these books within the year, and in the right chronological order. So what did I make of 'The Sinner'? Well, unfortunately I am disappointed to have to report that I found it much weaker and far less appealing than the previous novels as it felt like going 'one step forward, two steps back'. Like the other books, the opening was very strong, interesting and original, setting the scene and adding the highly sought after mystery factor which gave me a certain eagerness to continue to discover the jewels and delights contained within its covers. And then the similarity ended. This book had a good solid storyline, with some interesting characters, but the emphasis of the story seemed to be based more upon the romantic lives of the two main protagonists rather than on the thrills and excitement of the medical, murder, mystery adventure itself. A big, big let-down. So much so that in this story Dr Isles appears to be leading the police investigation rather than the irritating, cold and constantly moaning 'tomboy' Rizzoli who seems more preoccupied about her image and private life rather than getting on and actually solving the different elements of the case set before her. Yes, too much 'best seller' romantic distracting 'mush' for me and not enough rough, tough action or the deeper development of actual events set around the crimes themselves. More emphasis given to the initial events, the Nun's lives (especially the Abbess), life in the convent and the role of the Church itself would have been fascinating and added much value to the journey rather than concentrating on ridiculous, blind relationships (Isles and the Priest - how(?)), personal issues, overtly melodramatic pieces of dialogue and vague, slightly far-fetched distractions that detracted from the pleasure and enjoyment of the overall complete reading experience. <br />So generally, where does that now leave me regarding my mission? Well, my interest has unfortunately waned but the storylines, characters and medical police procedures offered by the author still appeal enough for me to continue with the series, but this excursion did feel like a slight 'knock' and the noticeably negative change of focus of emphasising and concentrating on the private lives of these personalities rather than the murder mystery thriller aspect didn't quite cut it enough for me. Anyway, let's see what book 4 provides and just hope that the series returns to its earlier winning formula whilst providing that 'feel good factor' to the reader. Time will tell, fingers are crossed, but things, right now, are definitely in the balance. I hope I touch lucky. Rating - 3.2 stars.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="505127205690764191" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brenda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brenda" href="/user/show/2337007-brenda">Brenda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Tess Gerritsen/thriller lovers</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2337007-brenda?shelf=own-read">own-read</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer195480052" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1204621107871439124">When Dr Maura Isles was called to the chapel of Our Lady of Divine Light by Detective Jane Rizzoli, she wasn’t sure what to expect. But it certainly wasn’t the horrific, savage attack on two nuns, one of whom is dead, the other clinging to life. And medical examiner Maura was further shocked when doing the autopsy, to discover that the young novice, 20 year old Sister Camille, had very recently given birth. <br/><br/>The race is on to find the child, and to find the father...obviously he is a suspect! But</span>
  <span id="freeText1204621107871439124" style="display:none">When Dr Maura Isles was called to the chapel of Our Lady of Divine Light by Detective Jane Rizzoli, she wasn’t sure what to expect. But it certainly wasn’t the horrific, savage attack on two nuns, one of whom is dead, the other clinging to life. And medical examiner Maura was further shocked when doing the autopsy, to discover that the young novice, 20 year old Sister Camille, had very recently given birth. <br /><br />The race is on to find the child, and to find the father...obviously he is a suspect! But was it consensual or was it rape? With Jane talking to young Noni, daughter of the cook/housekeeper of Our Lady of Divine Light, she finds some surprising clues. Though Noni is a child, she is very observant, a silent watcher in the nunnery.<br /><br />When another body is found, mutilated beyond recognition, little did they realize that the two murders were connected, that there was an ancient disaster that had lain hidden for decades, and suddenly, as these secrets begin to come to light, Maura finds herself in danger. The investigation starts to feel incredibly close to home. Will Jane and Maura be able to find the killer before they themselves are in deep trouble? <br /><br />The incredible twists that Gerritsen can weave throughout her novels keeps the pages turning, the dark and frightening traits to human behaviour leaving you shocked to the core!<br /><br />Another thoroughly enjoyable Gerritsen thriller!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1204621107871439124" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText826339669137246111" style="display:none">This book was good but not great. The author went to great lengths to develop her characters, but there is a limit to how much you can accomplish in one novel. Granted, there is a payoff for this type of character development in later novels when the reader is attached to them. This novel has a great story that is forced into the background by the information dump of the personal lives of the characters.<br />Even the mystery itself seems to be created to develop the characters. I plan to continue reading this series, and for people that choose to do so (and I do recommend it)this book will become required reading in order to fully understand the main characters but is not the most interesting to read.<br />Four stars because the author is so talented it shows through the plot's murkiness.</span>

<div id="review_1081588007" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1081588007" />
    <a title="Siobhan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35855553-siobhan"><img alt="Siobhan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1510311895p2/35855553.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1081588007?book_show_action=true">Oct 16, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Siobhan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Siobhan" href="/user/show/35855553-siobhan">Siobhan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1081588007" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3716578757003367592">The third Rizzoli and Isles book and another brilliant read.<br/><br/>If you have read the first two Rizzoli and Isles books then you should know that Gerritsen knows how to weave a great story, keeping things interesting throughout, carrying the story on. In this book we get a deeper insight into the life of Isles – something that will please many people as she has been a bit of an enigma up until this book. Due to this there are, once again, the signs of Gerritsen’s past romance books to be found yet it</span>
  <span id="freeText3716578757003367592" style="display:none">The third Rizzoli and Isles book and another brilliant read.<br /><br />If you have read the first two Rizzoli and Isles books then you should know that Gerritsen knows how to weave a great story, keeping things interesting throughout, carrying the story on. In this book we get a deeper insight into the life of Isles – something that will please many people as she has been a bit of an enigma up until this book. Due to this there are, once again, the signs of Gerritsen’s past romance books to be found yet it is not quite to the same degree as some of her work. <br /><br />One thing that disappointed me with this book (and may not have an effect on other people) is the lack of Special Agent Gabriel Dean. Following the ending of The Apprentice, I was expecting to see more of him in this book just to see where that story was heading. The lack of him plays in well with the storyline and the direction of the book, but a part of me wanted to know more about those particulars. As I said, though, I’m sure there are many people following the series who will not be affected by such a thing.<br /><br />I would also like to say that those who have watched the television series are in for quite a shock when reading the books. I was part way through the fourth book (Body Double) when I decided to start with the television series and there were many moments which left me shocked with the changes that were made. As is almost always the case, the books are so much better than the television series. Whether you have watched the show or are merely a crime fan looking for something more I would certainly recommend the Rizzoli and Isles series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3716578757003367592" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1268052492" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7432530710169478430">Talk about ickyness.<br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32257.The_Sinner__Rizzoli___Isles___3_' title='The Sinner (Rizzoli & Isles, #3) by Tess Gerritsen' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Sinner</a> is the third book of the Rizzoli and Isles series so it would be better if you read the first two books before reading this one. <br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32257.The_Sinner__Rizzoli___Isles___3_' title='The Sinner (Rizzoli & Isles, #3) by Tess Gerritsen' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Sinner</a> is <b>gruesome</b> and I loved it. I only hope that Gerritsen would settle down a bit with all the medical terms in her book. It's a bit too much and if I wasn't hooked with the story, I would have given up with this one.<br/><br/>There are some things in this book that'll either make you raise your eyebrows or it'll make the hair at your neck </span>
  <span id="freeText7432530710169478430" style="display:none">Talk about ickyness.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32257.The_Sinner__Rizzoli___Isles___3_" title="The Sinner (Rizzoli &amp; Isles, #3) by Tess Gerritsen" rel="nofollow noopener">The Sinner</a> is the third book of the Rizzoli and Isles series so it would be better if you read the first two books before reading this one. <br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32257.The_Sinner__Rizzoli___Isles___3_" title="The Sinner (Rizzoli &amp; Isles, #3) by Tess Gerritsen" rel="nofollow noopener">The Sinner</a> is <b>gruesome</b> and I loved it. I only hope that Gerritsen would settle down a bit with all the medical terms in her book. It's a bit too much and if I wasn't hooked with the story, I would have given up with this one.<br /><br />There are some things in this book that'll either make you raise your eyebrows or it'll make the hair at your neck raise.You decide if you'll be against it or go along with it. Icky stuffs like rotting bodies and missing limbs are perfectly normal in this book so toughen your stomach and your heart. Some stuff in this book is extreme.</span>

<div id="review_2655296348" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2655296348" />
    <a title="Iza Brekilien" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9607392-iza-brekilien"><img alt="Iza Brekilien" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580847624p2/9607392.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2655296348?book_show_action=true">Jan 24, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Iza Brekilien" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Iza Brekilien" href="/user/show/9607392-iza-brekilien">Iza Brekilien</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9607392-iza-brekilien?shelf=mystery-suspense-thriller">mystery-suspense-thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2655296348" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6580225908761140953">I really liked it, but not as much as the first two books. It was written differently, not only from Jane's point of view, but also from Maura's. There were as much personal issues than actual police affair. <br/><br/>My problem was that it felt like a police novel written for women (maybe it is, after all ?), that is to say : with the label "romance inside". Not that I don't like romance, but there was too much romance : I didn't like Victor, didn't like that he did what he did and went away from it with</span>
  <span id="freeText6580225908761140953" style="display:none">I really liked it, but not as much as the first two books. It was written differently, not only from Jane's point of view, but also from Maura's. There were as much personal issues than actual police affair. <br /><br />My problem was that it felt like a police novel written for women (maybe it is, after all ?), that is to say : with the label "romance inside". Not that I don't like romance, but there was too much romance : I didn't like Victor, didn't like that he did what he did and went away from it with his conscience clear, still loving Maura it seems, while another man seemed interested in Maura too, and she in him but with no real reason. Too much. I almost prefered Jane's story, with her doubts, her family, her courage and her issues. She's straightforward, rough, and I like that.<br /><br />And I appreciated the story of the murders and what went on, I never would have thought of it at the beginning, very nice ! </span>
  <a data-text-id="6580225908761140953" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1735689192" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1735689192" />
    <a title="Nancy Brady" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2870158-nancy-brady"><img alt="Nancy Brady" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1359132338p2/2870158.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1735689192?book_show_action=true">Aug 22, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nancy Brady" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nancy Brady" href="/user/show/2870158-nancy-brady">Nancy Brady</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780345458926" href="/book/show/841179.The_Sinner">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2870158-nancy-brady?shelf=from-another-bookcrosser">from-another-bookcrosser</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1735689192" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11930133990630764965">4.5 stars...this suspense-filled tale finds Jane Rizzoli and Maura Isles working together to figure why two nuns in a cloistered convent were brutally beaten and killed. Added into this stress is the murder of a Jane Doe, and individual issues for each of the two main characters.<br/><br/>Putting it all together before anyone else is killed will push them to the edge especially as their own issues may play a part. <br/> <br/>Having read these out of order does not affect the enjoyment of the novel. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('c4XaNxh5hguc8OwTX63JYwWlcp0xUca9XpUf5qLjwpMvBRH/Zh46HaSYsmTzmORomwwY7jY+9TQR0cn2dzGvAg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('3Kd5G/+8yOjLa5hskNTM4+eOtHiI4VKbs9ByYO/FNPWAJ7LTgdt0/vMDxhs84eHoeSfeC4+OYRL8lKRwOhdZZA==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer4168520593229881437">Internationally bestselling author Tess Gerritsen took an unusual route to a writing career. A graduate of Stanford University, Tess went on to medical school at the University of California, San Francisco, where she was awarded her M.D.<br/><br/>While on maternity leave from her work as a physician, she began to write fiction. In 1987, her first novel was published. Call After Midnight, a romantic thriller</span>
  <span id="freeText4168520593229881437" style="display:none">Internationally bestselling author Tess Gerritsen took an unusual route to a writing career. A graduate of Stanford University, Tess went on to medical school at the University of California, San Francisco, where she was awarded her M.D.<br /><br />While on maternity leave from her work as a physician, she began to write fiction. In 1987, her first novel was published. Call After Midnight, a romantic thriller, was followed by eight more romantic suspense novels. She also wrote a screenplay, "Adrift", which aired as a 1993 CBS Movie of the Week starring Kate Jackson.<br /><br />Tess's first medical thriller, Harvest, was released in hardcover in 1996, and it marked her debut on the New York Times bestseller list. Her suspense novels since then have been: Life Support (1997), Bloodstream (1998), Gravity (1999), The Surgeon (2001), The Apprentice (2002), The Sinner (2003), Body Double (2004), Vanish (2005), The Mephisto Club (2006), and The Bone Garden (2007). Her books have been translated into 31 languages, and more than 15 million copies have been sold around the world.<br /><br />As well as being a New York Times bestselling author, she has also been a #1 bestseller in both Germany and the UK. She has won both the Nero Wolfe Award (for Vanish) and the Rita Award (for The Surgeon.) Critics around the world have praised her novels as "Pulse-pounding fun" (Philadelphia Inquirer), "Scary and brilliant" (Toronto Globe and Mail), and "Polished, riveting prose" (Chicago Tribune). Publisher Weekly has dubbed her the "medical suspense queen".<br /><br />Now retired from medicine, she writes full time. She lives in Maine.</span>

Police can only assume an acolyte is at large, a maniac basing his attacks on the twisted medical techniques of the madman he so admires. At least that\'s what Detective Jane Rizzoli thinks.
